# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM IR Type System to Code Generation Chain

## Your Task

Trace how LLVM IR types flow from the type creation API to code generation in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files implementing: the Type class hierarchy (IntegerType, FunctionType, StructType), the type system's context ownership, and the IR type to machine type lowering in SelectionDAG.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the LLVM IR type system flow from creation to code generation. The answer document at `/workspace/answer.json` includes:

## Summary of Findings

**Key Files Identified (10 total)**:
1. **Type Class Definitions**: `llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h`, `DerivedTypes.h`
2. **Type Implementations**: `llvm/lib/IR/Type.cpp`
3. **Context & Storage**: `llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h` 
4. **Value Types**: `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/ValueTypes.h`
5. **Target Lowering**: `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h`
6. **SelectionDAG**: `SelectionDAGBuilder.cpp`, `LegalizeTypes.cpp`, `SelectionDAG.h`

**Complete Type Flow Chain**:

1. **Type Creation API** → `Type::getInt32Ty()`, `IntegerType::get()`, `FunctionType::get()`, `StructType::create()`
2. **Context Ownership** → Types stored in `LLVMContextImpl` with uniquing via `DenseSet` + `KeyInfo` structs
3. **SelectionDAGBuilder** → Converts `Type*` to `EVT` via `TargetLowering::getValueType()`
4. **EVT (Extended Value Type)** → Bridges LLVM IR types to machine types, handles arbitrary-width types
5. **Type Legalization** → `DAGTypeLegalizer` transforms non-legal EVTs to legal ones (Promotion, Expansion, etc.)
6. **Machine Type Lowering** → Maps to register types via `TargetLowering` tables

The analysis includes detailed code examples, design patterns (type uniquing, context ownership, immutability), and a complete flow example tracing how an `i32` parameter flows through the entire system.

Also note that only one instance of a particular\\n39: /// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\\n40: /// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\\n41: /// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\\n42: /// in class Type and in derived classes. Also note that only one instance of a particular\n39: /// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\n40: /// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\n41: /// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\n42: /// in class Type and in derived classes.  Once allocated, Types are never\n43: /// free'd.\n44: ///\n45: class Type {\n46: public:\n47:   //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n48:   /// Definitions of all of the base types for the Type system.  Based on this\n49:   /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n50:   /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n51:   /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n52:   /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n53:   ///\n54:   enum TypeID {\n55:     // PrimitiveTypes\n56:     HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n57:     BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n58:     FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n59:     DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n60:     X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n61:     FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n62:     PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n63:     VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n64:     LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n65:     MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n66:     X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n67:     TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n68: \n69:     // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n70:     IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n71:     FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n72:     PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n73:     StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n74:     ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n75:     FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n76:     ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n77:     TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n78:     TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n79:   };\n80: \n81: private:\n82:   /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n83:   LLVMContext &Context;\n84: \n85:   TypeID   ID : 8; Type Class Hierarchy\\n\\n### Base Type Class (llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h)\\nThe `Type` class is the base class for all LLVM IR types.  // Maps VT to register type\\n}\\n```\\n\\nTarget subclasses override type action tables:\\n- `ValueTypeActions`: Maps EVT \u2192 legal action (Promote/Expand/LibCall/etc.)\\n- `RegisterTypeForVT`: Maps MVT \u2192 register type\\n- `NumRegistersForVT`: Maps MVT \u2192 number of registers needed\\n\\n## 4. SelectionDAG Node Type System\\n\\n**Location**: llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAG.h, llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAG.cpp\\n\\nSelectionDAG nodes use EVT to track value types:\\n- Each SDNode has value types in SDVTList\\n- SDValue wraps (SDNode*, ResNo) and provides `.getValueType()` returning EVT\\n- Type information flows through DAG optimization and legalization passes\\n\\nSelectionDAG provides EVT-aware helpers:\\n```cpp\\nSDValue getValueType(EVT);  // Creates constant SDNode with type value\\nEVT getEVTAlign(EVT VT);    // Converts EVT to alignment\\n```\\n\\n## 5. Complete Flow Example\\n\\nFor a function parameter of type `i32`:\\n\\n1. **IR Level**: `Type::getInt32Ty(Context)` returns cached IntegerType instance\\n2. **Context Ownership**: Stored in `Context.pImpl->Int32Ty`\\n3. **SelectionDAGBuilder**: Calls `TLI.getValueType(DL, Type::getInt32Ty(...))`\\n4. **EVT Creation**: `EVT::getEVT()` returns MVT::i32 wrapped in EVT\\n5. **Legalization**: LegalizeTypes checks if i32 is legal (typically yes)\\n6. **RegisterTypes**: TargetLowering maps i32 \u2192 GPR type (e.g., MVT::i64 on 64-bit targets)\\n7. **Code Generation**: SelectionDAG uses EVT through all DAG combines, lowering, and ISel\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **Type Uniquing**: All types are uniqued in LLVMContext, enabling pointer comparison\\n2. **Context Ownership**: All types belong to a single LLVMContext lifetime\\n3. **Immutability**: Types are immutable after creation (thread-safe)\\n4. **Lazy Legalization**: Types are only legalized when needed during SelectionDAG processing\\n5. **Target-Aware Lowering**: TargetLowering translates IR types to target-specific machine types\\n6. **Extended Value Types**: EVT bridges LLVM IR types and machine value types for arbitrary-width types\\n\"\n}\n",

 // Maps VT to register type\\n}\\n```\\n\\nTarget subclasses override type action tables:\\n- `ValueTypeActions`: Maps EVT \u2192 legal action (Promote/Expand/LibCall/etc.)\\n- `RegisterTypeForVT`: Maps MVT \u2192 register type\\n- `NumRegistersForVT`: Maps MVT \u2192 number of registers needed\\n\\n## 4. SelectionDAG Node Type System\\n\\n**Location**: llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAG.h, llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAG.cpp\\n\\nSelectionDAG nodes use EVT to track value types:\\n- Each SDNode has value types in SDVTList\\n- SDValue wraps (SDNode*, ResNo) and provides `.getValueType()` returning EVT\\n- Type information flows through DAG optimization and legalization passes\\n\\nSelectionDAG provides EVT-aware helpers:\\n```cpp\\nSDValue getValueType(EVT);  // Creates constant SDNode with type value\\nEVT getEVTAlign(EVT VT);    // Converts EVT to alignment\\n```\\n\\n## 5. Complete Flow Example\\n\\nFor a function parameter of type `i32`:\\n\\n1. **IR Level**: `Type::getInt32Ty(Context)` returns cached IntegerType instance\\n2. **Context Ownership**: Stored in `Context.pImpl->Int32Ty`\\n3. **SelectionDAGBuilder**: Calls `TLI.getValueType(DL, Type::getInt32Ty(...))`\\n4. **EVT Creation**: `EVT::getEVT()` returns MVT::i32 wrapped in EVT\\n5. **Legalization**: LegalizeTypes checks if i32 is legal (typically yes)\\n6. **RegisterTypes**: TargetLowering maps i32 \u2192 GPR type (e.g., MVT::i64 on 64-bit targets)\\n7. **Code Generation**: SelectionDAG uses EVT through all DAG combines, lowering, and ISel\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **Type Uniquing**: All types are uniqued in LLVMContext, enabling pointer comparison\\n2. **Context Ownership**: All types belong to a single LLVMContext lifetime\\n3. **Immutability**: Types are immutable after creation (thread-safe)\\n4. **Lazy Legalization**: Types are only legalized when needed during SelectionDAG processing\\n5. **Target-Aware Lowering**: TargetLowering translates IR types to target-specific machine types\\n6. **Extended Value Types**: EVT bridges LLVM IR types and machine value types for arbitrary-width types\\n\"\n}\n",
